      <p><b>Canada</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:EN-CA-Canada.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/EN-CA-Canada.ogg" class="internal" title="EN-CA-Canada.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ka.na.dɑ]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. It is north of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Its land reaches from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> in the east to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a> to the north. Canada's area is 9.98&nbsp;million square kilometres (3.85&nbsp;million square miles), so it is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">second largest country by total area</a> but only the fourth largest country by <a href="/wiki/Land_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Land area">land area</a>. It has the world's longest <a href="/wiki/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastline">coastline</a> which touches three <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">oceans</a>. Canada has <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">ten provinces and three territories</a>. Most parts of the country have a cold or severely cold <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a> <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a>, but areas to the south are warm in <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summer</a>. Much of the land is <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> towards the west. About four fifths of Canada's 36 million people live in <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urban areas</a> near the southern border with the US, the longest between any two countries in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">national capital</a> is <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, and the largest <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>. Other large cities include <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Aboriginal people">Aboriginal people</a> lived in the places that are now Canada for a long time. In 1537 the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> started a colony and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> soon followed. The two empires fought several wars and in the late 18th century only <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> remained with what is more or less Canada today. The country was formed with the <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_North_America_Act&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="British North America Act (not yet started)">British North America Act</a> on July 1, 1867, from several colonies. Over time, more provinces and territories became part of Canada. In 1931, Canada achieved near total independence with the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a>, and became <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">completely independent</a> when the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada_Act_1982&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canada Act 1982 (not yet started)">Canada Act 1982</a> removed the last remaining ties of legal dependence on the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>. </p>
      <p>Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom</a> as its head of state. The country is officially <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a> at the federal level, meaning that <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizens</a> have the right to communicate with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">government</a> in either English or French. <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">Immigration to Canada</a> has made it one of the world's most ethnically diverse and <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism_in_Canada" title="Multiculturalism in Canada">multicultural</a> nations. Its economy is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">the eleventh largest in the world</a>, and relies mainly on <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a> and well-developed international <a href="/wiki/Trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Trading">trade networks</a>. Canada's relationship with its neighbor and biggest trading partner, the U.S., has a big impact on its <a href="/w/index.php?title=Economy_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Economy of Canada (not yet started)">economy</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Culture_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Culture of Canada (not yet started)">culture</a>. </p>
      <p>Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">tenth highest</a> nominal per capita income globally as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">tenth highest</a> ranking in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. It ranks among the highest in international measurements of government transparency, <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, quality of life, economic freedom, and education. Canada is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a> member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie</a>, and part of several major international and intergovernmental institutions or groupings including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=G-20_major_economies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="G-20 major economies (not yet started)">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation (not yet started)">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> forum. </p>

       </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>By total area (including its waters), Canada is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">second-largest country</a> in the world, after Russia. By land area alone, Canada <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_land_area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of countries and outlying territories by land area (not yet started)">ranks fourth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-12">[11]</a></sup> It has the longest border with water (<a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coastline</a>) of any country in the world. It is next to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> Oceans. It is the only country in the world to be next to three oceans at once. It has six <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Canada is made up of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories">ten provinces and three territories</a>. The provinces are between the 45th and 60th parallels of latitude, and the territories are to the north of the 60th parallel of latitude. Most large cities in Canada are in the southern part of the country, including Toronto, Vancouver, and Montreal. There are very few people living in the northern part of Canada. </p>
      <p>Canada extends from the west coast, across the <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairies</a> and central Canada, to the Atlantic provinces. In the north there are three territories, between Alaska and Greenland: the Yukon in the west, then the Northwest Territories, then Nunavut. Four of the five <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> (Superior, Huron, Erie, and Ontario) are shared between Canada and the United States (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">Lake Michigan</a> is in the <a href="/wiki/USA" class="mw-redirect" title="USA">USA</a>), and they make up 16% of the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Seaway" title="Saint Lawrence Seaway">Saint Lawrence Seaway</a> joins the Great Lakes to the Atlantic Ocean, allowing ocean going vessels to travel as far inland as <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay,_Ontario" class="mw-redirect" title="Thunder Bay, Ontario">Thunder Bay</a> in Ontario, Canada. </p>
      <p>Canada shares land and sea borders with the USA (the lower 48 states and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>), <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>), and France (St. Pierre and Miquelon — a small group of islands off the southern coast off the island of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>). </p>
      <p>The geography of Canada is very different from place to place, from high <a href="/wiki/Alpine_tundra" title="Alpine tundra">alpine areas</a> in the west, flat <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> and prairies in the centre, and ancient <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shield_(geology)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shield (geology) (not yet started)">shield</a> rocks in the east. Canada contains some of the very last untouched <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Boreal forest">boreal forest</a> in the world. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> is a vast area of ancient Pre-Cambrian rocks lying in an arc around <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>, covering more than one third of Canada's land area. This is a unique land of lakes, bogs, swamps, trees, and rocks. It is a terrain that is very dangerous and difficult to traverse cross country because of lakes, bogs, swamps, trees, and rocks. Canada has 60% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="History of Canada (not yet started)">History of Canada</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aboriginal_peoples">Aboriginal peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Aboriginal peoples">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Aboriginal peoples">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">Indigenous peoples</a> lived in what is now Canada for thousands of years before the first Europeans arrived. The indigenous groups are called the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis" class="mw-redirect" title="Métis">Métis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GraberKuprecht2012_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GraberKuprecht2012-15">[14]</a></sup> The Métis are people that come from both <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> and European families.<sup id="cite_ref-GraberKuprecht2012_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GraberKuprecht2012-15">[14]</a></sup> Together, these three groups are called "Indigenous," "Aboriginal," or "First Peoples." They used to be called "Indians" by the Europeans, but this is now considered rude. </p>
      <p>Many people think that the first people to live in Canada came from <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> by using the <a href="/wiki/Bering_land_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Bering land bridge">Bering land bridge</a> at least 14,000 years ago. The land bridge used to connect Asia and North America.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FaganDurrani2016_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FaganDurrani2016-17">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When European people first came to Canada to <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">settle</a>, the number of Indigenous people living in Canada already was between 200,000 and two million.<sup id="cite_ref-dying_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dying-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steckel_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steckel-19">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">European colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: European colonization">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: European colonization">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> were the first Europeans known to land in what is now called Canada, in what is now <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, led by the Viking explorer <a href="/wiki/Leif_Erikson" title="Leif Erikson">Leif Erikson</a>. They did not stay long, however. In the early 16th century, Europeans started exploring Canada's eastern coast, beginning with <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> from <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> in 1497, and later <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">Jacques Cartier</a> in 1534 from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Mackenzie" class="mw-disambig" title="Alexander Mackenzie">Alexander Mackenzie</a> later reached the Pacific coast over land, where captains <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Vancouver" title="George Vancouver">George Vancouver</a> went by sea. The Europeans also traded beaver furs to the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>Parts of Canada were settled by France, and parts by <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>. In 1605, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Port-Royal_(Acadia)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Port-Royal (Acadia) (not yet started)">Port-Royal</a> was built in Acadia (today called Nova Scotia) by the French, led by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">Samuel de Champlain</a>, and in 1608 he started settling Quebec. The British took control of the French areas after a battle of the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plains_of_Abraham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plains of Abraham (not yet started)">Plains of Abraham</a> near <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a> in 1759. </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, many people in the new <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> wanted to stay loyal to Britain. Thousands came north to Canada and settled in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>. They were called <a href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalists" title="United Empire Loyalists">United Empire Loyalists</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, the United States tried to conquer Canada but were defeated. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Confederation_and_expansion">Confederation and expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Confederation and expansion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Confederation and expansion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On July 1, 1867, Canada was united under a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal government</a>. It included the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/John_A._Macdonald" title="John A. Macdonald">John A. Macdonald</a> was the first prime minister. <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> territory, and the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a> became part of Canada in 1870. <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> joined in 1871, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a> in 1873. </p>
      <p>There were two <a href="/wiki/Red_River_Rebellion" title="Red River Rebellion">Red River Rebellions</a>, in 1869-70 and 1885, both led by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Riel" title="Louis Riel">Louis Riel</a>. He fought for more <a href="/wiki/Rights" title="Rights">rights</a> for the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people" title="Métis people">Métis people</a>, a mix between French and First Nations. A <a href="/wiki/Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Railroad">railroad</a> across the country, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">Canadian Pacific Railway</a>, finished in 1885, made it easier for Canadians to move to the west. Many Europeans came to the <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairies</a>, so <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a> became provinces in 1905. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Early 20th century">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Early 20th century">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Canadian soldiers fought in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> for the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. More Canadians died in this war than any other war. Canada became better known as a country after its success in capturing <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vimy_Ridge" title="Battle of Vimy Ridge">Vimy Ridge</a> from the Germans in France in 1917. Women were given the right to vote by the end of the war, partly because of the help they gave making weapons while the men fought in Europe. In 1931, Canada became fully <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independent</a>. Then the government of Canada made all decisions about Canada. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Crew of a Sherman-tank resting while parked" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/140px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/210px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg/280px-Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="3472"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Crew_of_a_Sherman-tank_south_of_Vaucelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Canadian crew during the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">battle of Normandy</a> in June 1944.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Canadians also fought in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dieppe_Raid" title="Dieppe Raid">Dieppe Raid</a> in 1942 went very badly and most of the soldiers were killed, wounded, or taken prisoner. Canadians were important in 1944 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Normandy" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Normandy">Normandy</a>, and they liberated the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> from the Germans. </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times">Modern times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Modern times">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Modern times">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1949, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a> became the 10th province of Canada. In 1956, Canadian <a href="/wiki/Lester_Pearson" class="mw-redirect" title="Lester Pearson">Lester Pearson</a>, who later became prime minister, helped end the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Suez_Crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Suez Crisis (not yet started)">Suez Crisis</a>. As a result, he won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>. In 1965, Pearson helped Canada get a new flag, the <a href="/wiki/Maple_Leaf" class="mw-redirect" title="Maple Leaf">Maple Leaf</a>. Before that, Canadians had used the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Canada" title="Flag of Canada">Red Ensign</a>. In 1982, Canada changed its <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a>, including a new <a href="/w/index.php?title=Canadian_Charter_of_Rights_and_Freedoms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms (not yet started)">Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms</a>. The main part of the Constitution is still the 1867 <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> Act. </p>
      <p>Some French Canadians today wish to form their own country, separate from the rest of Canada. The province of Quebec held a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="Referendum">referendum</a> (vote) in 1980, but only about 40% wanted to separate. Another referendum was held in 1995, with almost 50% voting in favour of leaving Canada. Since then, fewer people in Quebec have wanted to leave Canada, but it is still important to Quebec politics. </p>
      <p>Today, about 25% of Canadians speak French as their first language. Many people can speak both French and English. Although most French Canadians live in the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, there are French-speaking communities and people all across Canada. For example, 40% of the people in the province of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and 20% of those in <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> have a strong French background, as do some people in <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, mainly along its border with Quebec. </p>
      <p>In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> was created as Canada's third territory, out of the eastern <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, in an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> people. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_(14766251442).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg/200px-Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg/300px-Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg/400px-Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_%2814766251442%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5574" data-file-height="3448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Block_and_Centennial_Flame_(14766251442).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_Hill" title="Parliament Hill">Parliament Hill</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Canada has a government called a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a> (meaning a king or queen is the head of that country), and is a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> (meaning the people of that country rule it). The head of state is <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, who is officially the Queen of Canada. She appoints a <a href="/wiki/Governor_General" title="Governor General">Governor General</a> to represent her in the country, however, the choice of Governor General is made by the prime minister. </p>
      <p>The Queen's powers are mostly exercised by the Governor General, currently <a href="/wiki/Julie_Payette" title="Julie Payette">Julie Payette</a>. The Governor General, like the Canadian sovereign (King/Queen of Canada), is not political and remains above politics, and because of that they do not usually use their powers without the advice of the Prime Minister or other ministers. </p>
      <p>The head of government is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister</a>. The current prime minister is <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> who replaced <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Harper" title="Stephen Harper">Stephen Harper</a> in October 2015. Each province and territory has a <a href="/wiki/Premier" title="Premier">premier</a> to lead its government. The day-to-day operations of the government are run by the cabinet. The cabinet is usually formed from the largest party in Parliament. </p>
      <p>The Parliament of Canada passes the laws of the country. The governor general, acting on behalf of the monarch, has the right to <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> a law (meaning the law cannot go into effect) but this right has not been used for some time. There are five main parties in the Canadian Parliament: the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party" title="New Democratic Party">New Democratic Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberal Party</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Bloc_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Bloc Québécois">Bloc Québécois</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Canada" title="Green Party of Canada">Green Party</a>. In addition to the five parties with MPs in Parliament, there are fourteen other smaller parties registered with Elections Canada and several MPs who sit as Independents. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces_and_territories">Provinces and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Provinces and territories">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Provinces and territories">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_its_influence">Climate and its influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Climate and its influence">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Climate and its influence">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Many people from other parts of the world think of Canada as a very cold and snowy place. While it is true that much of Canada is very far north, most Canadians live in the southern parts, where the weather is much milder. Nearly two thirds of Canadians live less than 100 kilometres (62&nbsp;mi) from the U.S. border.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> In some cities the temperature can get very cold in the winter, especially in the inland.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Warm air systems moving in from the Pacific Ocean bring more rain than snow to the Pacific coast, while colder temperatures further inland do result in snow. Most of Canada can get quite hot in the summer, often over 30 degrees Celsius (86 degrees Fahrenheit).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Canadians are known to play winter sports such as <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarding</a>, and also enjoy many summer sports and games. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Natural resources">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Natural resources">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg/200px-Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg/300px-Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg/400px-Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4150" data-file-height="2467"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Peyto_Lake-Banff_NP-Canada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Peyto Lake in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Canada has lots of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>. Its large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> have been used for <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/century" class="extiw" title="wikt:century">centuries</a> for food and money. <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">Hydroelectric</a> power (electricity by water) is abundant because of Canada's many rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Forests of the west are used for wood. Besides these renewable resources, Canada has metal ores and oil <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/deposit" class="extiw" title="wikt:deposit">deposits</a>. Also, Canada is the leading exporter of <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminum" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Demographics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Demographics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Around 35 million people live in Canada. This is almost the same number as in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. About 80% of the Canadian population live in the southern parts of Canada since the climates are milder than the northern parts of Canada. </p>
      <p>A large number of <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> from almost every part of the world come to live in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> One example is the former <a href="/wiki/Governor_General" title="Governor General">Governor General</a> of Canada, <a href="/wiki/Micha%C3%ABlle_Jean" title="Michaëlle Jean">Michaëlle Jean</a>, who came to Canada as a young child with her family from <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> in 1968. Today, up to 1/5th of the population is an immigrant to Canada. </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Healthcare">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Healthcare">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian government">Canadian government</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">provinces</a> are responsible for <a href="/w/index.php?title=Health_insurance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Health insurance (not yet started)">health insurance</a>. Five provinces prohibit all <a href="/w/index.php?title=Extra-billing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Extra-billing (not yet started)">extra-billing</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a> allow it in a small number of circumstances, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> do not restrict it at all.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2020 the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation</a> reported a deterioration in the number of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Acute_care_bed&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Acute care bed (not yet started)">acute care beds</a> available in <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospitals</a> per every 1,000 people in that province. Ontario is Canada's largest province, and is home to Canada's largest city, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>. The number of hospital beds available in Ontario is 1.4 per every 1,000 people. This is half the number hospitals beds available in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and the same number available in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>

      <p><b>Notes</b> </p> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-Anthem-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-Anthem_2-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Canada's de facto <a href="/wiki/Royal_anthem" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal anthem">royal anthem</a> is "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>", which is sometimes played or sung together with the national anthem, "O Canada", at private and public events. Additionally, its first three lines are also included within the "Viceregal Salute", which is accorded to the governor general and provincial lieutenant governors. However, it has never been adopted as an official symbol of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
      </ol>
